All turns stopped at results/availability — no login, no payment, no PII. **Updated tally vs opener Stage 7:** 3 of 4 hotel/booking sites reached REAL availability/results via agent turns; BA loads real content (fare-search not driven); Trainline blocked by a site-inventory gap + P6-41.

### P6-41 — Host `browser` tool: hrefless SPA *submit* navigation blocked by the SSRF guard (6c.6)
**Type:** finding/limitation · **Opened:** 6c.6 post-review (2026-06-13) · **Status:** OPEN — workaround in place; resolve at 6c.7.
On Trainline, the agent's ref- AND selector-based click on the "Find tickets" **submit** button (an hrefless React SPA button that triggers a client-side navigation to `/book/results`) returned *"Navigation blocked: strict browser SSRF policy requires an IP-literal URL …"* — even though `thetrainline.com` is allowlisted. **NOT a general click-nav failure:** click-through on a real `<a href>` link to an allowlisted host works (verified at CLI). The block hits when the guard **cannot pre-resolve the navigation target to an allowlisted hostname** before the click — i.e. JS/SPA navigations with no resolvable href (and likely any redirect chain that transits a non-allowlisted host, since `assertBrowserNavigationRedirectChainAllowed` validates every hop). **Impact:** reaching *results/availability* is fine (direct-URL or same-page interaction); progressing a booking via an hrefless "Continue/Select" SPA button may be blocked → matters for true pre-payment depth on SPA-heavy sites.
- **Workaround (works today):** navigate by **direct URL** (construct the results/availability URL with query params) instead of clicking the SPA submit; same-page widget interaction via selector/ref clicks.
- **6c.7 fix options (A-12, decide empirically):** (a) a tool/policy option to permit click-driven navigation when the *current page* host is allowlisted (trust same-origin SPA nav); (b) relax the redirect-chain check to the final landing host if allowlisted; (c) document direct-URL as the standard agent pattern. Keep the allowlist guarantee for cross-origin.
- **RESOLVED at 6c.7 by dissolution → see [P6-42].** Empirical recon of the guard (`assertBrowserNavigationAllowed` + `assertBrowserNavigationRedirectChainAllowed` in `dist/cdp.helpers-*.js`) confirmed the "requires IP-literal" error is simply a **non-allowlisted-host rejection on some redirect hop** (`www.google.com` reproduces it; allowlisted hosts pass). Peter elected to **renounce the hostname allowlist entirely** (unmaintainable; had already blocked Trenitalia). With the allowlist empty + the Gate-1 patch (P6-42), **no public host or redirect hop can be off-list**, so the P6-41 block is structurally impossible — click-driven SPA navigation to any public host now passes (verified: Trenitalia/Wikipedia navigations, which traverse redirects, succeed). No SPA-specific patch needed; options (a)/(b) moot. Residual friction on deep booking flows is **UI-automation robustness** (controlled date pickers), not a trust block → see [P6-44].

### P6-40 — Bundled browser-plugin runtime dep (`playwright-core`) not resolvable from gateway level — host fix (6c.6)
**Type:** finding + host fix · **Opened:** 6c.6 (2026-06-13) · **Status:** RESOLVED (workaround in place) — **fragile across `openclaw update`**.
On first use the gateway browser tool failed: *"Playwright is not available in this gateway build; … install playwright-core, then restart the gateway."* Root cause: `playwright-core@1.59.1` **is** bundled but ONLY under `dist/extensions/browser/node_modules/`; the importer `dist/pw-ai-C9c1nNLg.js` sits at `dist/` level, so Node's module walk-up (`dist/node_modules` → pkg-root `node_modules` → global) never reaches the nested copy → `ERR_MODULE_NOT_FOUND`. The availability probe (`getPwAiModule({mode:"soft"})`) **memoises the failed import for the gateway's lifetime**, so a restart is mandatory after the fix. The vendor `ensureBundledPluginRuntimeDeps` is a no-op here (reads a manifest field, not `package.json.dependencies`).
- **Fix applied:** symlink `…/openclaw/node_modules/playwright-core` → `…/dist/extensions/browser/node_modules/playwright-core` (reuses the bundled version-exact copy; no download; reversible) → gateway restart. Verified: `pw-ai` module imports, `snapshot`/`navigate` work.
- **CARRY:** an `openclaw update` (or reinstall) will wipe the symlink → browser tool breaks until re-applied. **Re-apply step** belongs in the runbook / a one-touch script. `@modelcontextprotocol/sdk` is also unresolved but only needed for the `existing-session` (Chrome-DevTools-MCP) driver, not our `openclaw`/CDP driver — left as-is.
- **RESOLVED durably at 6c.7.** One-touch repair script `~/.openclaw/scripts/browser-dep-repair.sh` (zsh, SSH-safe, idempotent): re-creates the symlink, restarts the gateway only if it changed, verifies with a real `navigate`. **Tested by simulation** — `unlink` the symlink → `gateway restart` reproduced the exact "Playwright is not available" failure → script repaired + verified (exit 0); a second run is a clean no-op. Extended to also re-apply the **P6-42** guard patch (locates the guard file by content since its hashed name changes across versions; excludes `.orig` backups), and verifies BOTH halves (public-site navigates + private-IP refused). Full update-wipe (rm symlink + revert guard) → script restored both. Wired into runbook **§2.13** + the §2.0 symptom map. **Run after every `openclaw update`.** Script sha `30899bb59d4e`/5294B.

### P6-42 — Renounce the host-browser domain allowlist → IP-class SSRF filtering (6c.7)
**Type:** decision + implementation (security posture) · **Opened+Resolved:** 6c.7 (2026-06-13) · **Decided by Peter.** Supersedes the allowlist-as-trust-routing framing of [P6-39]; dissolves [P6-41].
**Problem.** The 6c.6 `browser.ssrfPolicy.hostnameAllowlist` was repurposed as an enumerated "trusted websites" list. It is **operationally unworkable** — the open web can't be enumerated — and had already blocked Marie from Trenitalia. Peter elected to renounce it, deferring the security mechanics to Claude.
**Empirical guard analysis (A-12, read the 2026.4.22 build).** The native browser guard (`dist/cdp.helpers-*.js` → `ssrf-*.js`) has **two layers**: **Gate 1** (`isExplicitlyAllowedBrowserHostname`) is a DNS-rebinding pre-filter — for the host browser it treats an **empty** `hostnameAllowlist` as **deny-all** (require IP-literal), which is what forces enumeration. **Gate 2** (`resolvePinnedHostnameWithPolicy`) resolves the host and **blocks any private/internal/loopback/link-local/reserved IP independently of the allowlist** — this is the layer that actually protects the machine/LAN. Key facts: no universal wildcard is expressible (`normalizeHostnameAllowlist` strips `*`/`*.`; `isHostnameAllowedByPattern` only does exact or `*.suffix`); the only config lever to open Gate 1 is `dangerouslyAllowPrivateNetwork:true`, which **also disables Gate 2** (`shouldSkipPrivateNetworkChecks`) → all-or-nothing. So **no config-only "allow all public, block private" mode exists**; the CDP loopback connection self-exempts via `assertCdpEndpointAllowed`→`withAllowedHostname`, so emptying the list does **not** break gateway↔CDP.
**Change applied.** (1) Config `browser.ssrfPolicy.hostnameAllowlist = []` via `openclaw config set --strict-json` (gate-clear). (2) **One-token guard patch**: in `isExplicitlyAllowedBrowserHostname`, empty-list branch `… : false` → `… : true`, so an empty list **defers to Gate 2** instead of denying. `dangerouslyAllowPrivateNetwork` stays `false`. Net posture = **all PUBLIC hostnames allowed, all private/internal IPs blocked** — IP-class egress filtering, *strictly more secure* than the `dangerouslyAllowPrivateNetwork` escape hatch. Original guard backed up to `cdp.helpers-BWvLGafd.js.orig-6c7`; live guard sha `63e4284773ad`/22170B.
**Verified (CLI + real agent turn).** example.com/Trenitalia/Wikipedia (none previously listed) navigate ✓; `192.168.1.1` (LAN), `169.254.169.254` (metadata), `127.0.0.1:18800` (CDP) all **refused** ✓; gateway↔CDP intact ✓. **F26:** fresh Marie session, natural request → loaded Trenitalia, reported the real "CERCA" button, no pre-refusal. Agent docs (pa+pro TOOLS.md/AGENTS.md) rewritten: route by injection-trust to logged-in sessions, **not** by a site list; "blocked by policy" now means an internal IP only; **do not pre-refuse a public site from memory**.
**Update-fragility.** The guard patch lives in vendor `dist/` → wiped by `openclaw update`; re-apply folded into `browser-dep-repair.sh` ([P6-40]). **Reversible:** restore `.orig-6c7` + re-add a list.
**Residual risk (accepted, Peter):** an active DNS-rebind mid-session (Chrome re-resolving to a private IP) remains theoretically possible — true under the old allowlist too for any listed host — bounded by outbound/intentional use + the L1 consequential-action gates. The allowlist never defended the gift-card/value-exfiltration path anyway (attackers use reputable, listed sites) → that belongs to the **payment layer**, see [P6-45].

### P6-43 — Cold-path (F28) recovery depends on a GUI login; auto-login is OFF (6c.7)
**Type:** finding + decision-to-surface · **Opened:** 6c.7 (2026-06-13) · **Status:** OPEN — config-verified, live-reboot deferred (would strand the box; surfaced to Peter).
Verified the autostart chain **without** a disruptive live reboot (a reboot lands at the login window and, with auto-login off, downs the stack until someone logs in — irresponsible mid-session). Findings: gateway LaunchAgent `RunAtLoad=true`+`KeepAlive=true` ✓; `ai.openclaw.colima.plist` `RunAtLoad=true` ✓; sandbox containers `RestartPolicy=no` (brought up by the **gateway**, not Docker); `pmset autorestart=1` (powers back after outage), `sleep=0` (caffeinated). **Decisive gap:** gateway + Colima + headful Chrome are all **gui/502** (D20), and **auto-login is OFF** (`/Library/Preferences/com.apple.loginwindow` has no `autoLoginUser`) → a cold reboot does **not** self-recover headless; it needs a GUI login (manual/Screen-Sharing). **Free evidence it otherwise works:** this morning's restart recovered end-to-end (gateway pid changed, containers up ~7h, Chrome up, healthz 200) — i.e. a login had occurred.
- **DECISION for Peter (security tradeoff):** enable auto-login for `openclaw` → cold-path becomes fully unattended, **but** weakens at-rest security (boots straight into a logged-in session; interacts with FileVault). Alternatives: accept the "log in after reboot" operational step (documented), or a system-domain daemon (rejected — headful Chrome needs a display anyway). **Recommend:** decide auto-login vs documented-manual-login at 6c.8.
- **RESOLVED — ACCEPTED (Peter, 6c.7).** Auto-login **NOT pursued: FileVault is ON, and macOS disables auto-login under FileVault** — not trading away at-rest disk encryption. Mini reboots ~1–2×/month; on a cold boot it sits at the FileVault/login screen, **not remotely reachable** (Tailscale off; Screen Sharing needs a live session) → recovery is **physically at the machine**, as Peter has always done. **No dead-man's/uptime monitor** for now (it would only notify, not enable remote recovery — the actual constraint). Accepted posture: agents are down from a cold reboot until Peter physically logs in (acceptable at 1–2×/month). Revisit only if reboot frequency rises or remote recovery is wanted (would need Tailscale-at-boot + Remote Management). Document the manual step in runbook §2.1 at 6c.8.
- **6c.8 — DONE → CLOSED.** Manual cold-boot recovery documented in runbook §2.1 (FileVault-ON ⇒ cold boot halts at the unlock screen, `gui/502` LaunchAgents don't start, box unreachable; recover by console/Screen-Sharing login, FileVault Recovery Key in 1Password as fallback; ~1–2×/mo accepted, no auto-login, no uptime monitor). Decision implemented; entry closed.

### P6-44 — Complex-UI automation playbook (date pickers / multi-step forms) (6c.7)
**Type:** capability guidance · **Opened:** 6c.7 (2026-06-13) · **Status:** guidance landed in agent docs; per-site recipes on-demand.
Live deep-booking turns (Four Seasons, Booking.com) reached the availability/search form but stalled on **controlled React/Vue date pickers** (naive value-set ignored; click-through timed out) — a **UI-automation robustness** issue, **not** a trust/SSRF block (the agent twice *speculated* "SSRF" — a stale mental-model artefact, now corrected in docs). Recommendation (Peter's "simple-not-complex" preference): **defer** a general widget solver, **avoid** vision/coordinate clicking, **bank** two cheap wins — (1) a playbook in both agents' TOOLS.md (type-the-date-don't-click-the-calendar; encode search in the URL + `navigate`; `evaluate`+event-dispatch escape hatch; snapshot→act→verify; semantic verbs `fill`/`select`/`press`; never silently claim a policy block on a UI/timeout) and (2) **per-site recipes built on demand** for the ~6 sites actually used. Higher thinking level helps deep flows. Since L1 stops the agent at pre-payment, "the end" is only ~3–5 interactions deep per site.

### P6-45 — Payment-layer guardrail for the autonomy era (gate value, not browsing) (6c.7)
**Type:** forward design constraint · **Opened:** 6c.7 (2026-06-13) · **Status:** principle recorded for 6d/Andreas; no action now (L1 gate still in force).
Raised by Peter while reviewing [P6-42]: when full autonomy relaxes the L1 prepare-and-surface gate and an agent (e.g. Marie) holds a payment instrument, prompt-injection → irreversible purchase (gift cards = canonical cash-out; SCA exemptions for low-value/trusted-merchant/merchant-initiated transactions are the no-2FA gap). **Orthogonal to the browser allowlist** (an attacker uses reputable, would-be-listed sites). **Design constraint:** gate **value at the card issuer, not in the agent** — a dedicated virtual card with low per-tx/monthly caps + stored-value/quasi-cash MCC blocks (control sits outside the agent's trust boundary; injection can't argue with a decline); never fully remove the spend confirmation, raise its threshold as trust grows; optionally separate the session that ingests untrusted content from the one holding the card. Carry into the Andreas/6d autonomy work.

### P6-46 — Long agent turn → gateway timeout → stale session-lock wedges the agent (6c.7)
**Type:** finding/reliability · **Opened:** 6c.7 (2026-06-13) · **Status:** OPEN — recovery known (gateway restart); mitigations carried.
The deep Booking.com pre-payment turn (P6-44) ran the full ~8.5 min and hit the **gateway turn timeout (~510000ms)**. The cascade: gateway turn fails → CLI falls back to **embedded local** → the embedded run collides with the gateway's still-held lock on the **`agent:pa:main`** session jsonl (`…/sessions/<id>.jsonl.lock`, pid=gateway) → 10s lock-acquire timeout → model fallback to **`openai/gpt-4o`** (the below-tier `agents.defaults.model.fallbacks` entry the security audit flags) → `FailoverError`. **Live impact:** after the timeout the stale lock **wedged Marie's main session** — even a trivial new turn failed with "session file locked" until I **restarted the gateway**, which cleared the lane + lock (verified: Marie → "OK"). Note turns routed to `agent:pa:main` despite a distinct `--session-id`, so the contention isn't isolated by session-id.
- **Recovery:** `openclaw gateway restart` releases the stuck lane + lock (SSH-safe). If a `.lock` persists after restart, the orphaned lockfile can be removed (data is the `.jsonl`, not the `.lock`).
- **Mitigations (6c.8):** keep deep browser flows short (per-site recipes / direct-URL, P6-44) so turns finish well under the gateway timeout; consider a higher booking-turn timeout where justified; revisit the **gpt-4o fallback** (below-tier — security-audit WARN) and whether embedded-fallback-on-timeout should be suppressed for gateway agents to avoid the lock collision.
- **6c.8 update.** gpt-4o fallback **removed** — `agents.defaults.model.fallbacks` was set to `["anthropic/claude-sonnet-4-6"]` (drops the below-tier + injection-risk + rate-limited path); **later changed to `["openai/gpt-5"]` (universal cross-provider backup) — see [P6-58]**, which is the authoritative final fallback state. Caveat: Sonnet shares the same Anthropic workspace, so a *workspace*-level cap still kills both opus+sonnet → that case now surfaces **loudly** via the [P6-54] watchdog alert rather than degrading silently to an injection-prone model. Heartbeat turns are bounded by `timeoutSeconds:300`. (`skipWhenBusy` would directly guard the wedge but is **not in the 2026.4.22 heartbeat schema** — A-12 strict-json dry-run rejected it; carry for a future build / version.) Stale `.jsonl.lock` removal + restart recovery unchanged.

### P6-47 — Agent operational unreliability: root-cause diagnosis (8am reports / heartbeats failing) (6c.7 post-close)
**Type:** finding/diagnosis (reliability) · **Opened:** 6c.7 (2026-06-13) · **Status:** OPEN — diagnosis complete; fixes = the 6c.8 reliability sprint. Raised by Peter ("neither Marie nor Charlotte sending 8am reports, missing heartbeats, generally unreliable").
Evidence from `logs/gateway.log` + `logs/gateway.err.log` (the 8am report is **heartbeat-driven**, not a launchd/cron job — `cron` is deny-listed except for `cos`; `shared/daily-digests/` is empty since 15 May). Ranked root causes:
1. **🔴 LLM usage cap hit (dominant).** `gateway.err.log`: *"reached your specified workspace API usage limits. You will regain access on 2026-07-01 at 00:00 UTC."* → primary model (claude-opus-4-7) returns **HTTP 400** for the rest of June; every heartbeat/report that needs it is rejected. **Needs Peter's budget decision** (raise the Anthropic workspace cap / move agents to metered API billing / reduce consumption). NB: my own F26 test-turns this session spent the same limited budget — stopped.
2. **🔴 Broken fallback chain ([P6-46]).** Fallback `openai/gpt-4o` is below-tier **and** rate-limited (`Rate limit reached for gpt-4o` ×4) → no healthy degradation path. Replace with a Claude fallback (e.g. sonnet-4-6).
3. **🟠 Heartbeat loop stalls silently.** Beats fired 09:21–09:57 today then a **6-hour dead zone** to 16:11 while the gateway *process* stayed up (`KeepAlive` ≠ healthy beat loop). A wedged turn ([P6-46] session-lock) or provider rejection stalls it; **no watchdog** restarts it.
4. **🟠 Charlotte (`pro`) heartbeat DISABLED** (`openclaw status`) → no proactive Soveren triage at all. Re-enable with proper cadence (per her AGENTS.md / HEARTBEAT.md).
5. **🟠 Colima/Docker socket drops** — `Cannot connect to the Docker daemon` ×12 → sandbox unavailable → turns fail intermittently. Harden the gateway↔Colima socket.
6. **🟡 Missing daily memory files** — `ENOENT …/workspace-pa/memory/2026-…` ×8 (+pro ×3) breaks the heartbeat save step.
7. **🟡 Zero observability** — failures are silent (security-audit job parked `.disabled-D24`; nothing alerts Peter on a missed beat / unsent report). Add a heartbeat/report watchdog → Telegram.
8. ✅ Old SSRF blocks in the log (×14) — already resolved by [P6-42].
- **Recommendation:** 6c.8 = a **dedicated reliability-hardening sprint** (not capabilities), in dependency order (LLM unblock → fallback → heartbeat watchdog/Charlotte/Colima → observability). Andreas (CoS) sits on this stack — building him on it unhardened multiplies the flakiness.
- **RESOLVED — 6c.8 reliability sprint delivered.** (1) 🔴→✅ **LLM cap cleared:** Peter raised the production workspace cap $300→**$500** in the Anthropic Console; runtime-confirmed by one cheap Sonnet `capability model run --gateway` that answered `provider=anthropic model=claude-sonnet-4-6` with **zero failover attempts** (the 16:41/17:27 cooldown had cleared). (2) 🔴→✅ **fallback** → `claude-sonnet-4-6` ([P6-46]). (3) 🟠→✅ **heartbeat watchdog** live + stall-proven ([P6-54]). (4) 🟠→✅ **Charlotte re-enabled** ([P6-53]). (5) 🟠→🟡 **Colima socket:** root cause refined (`KeepAlive=false`) — carried to 6c.9 ([P6-57]). (6) 🟡→✅ **memory ENOENT:** today's `workspace-p{a,o}/memory/<date>.md` bootstrapped each watchdog run ([P6-54]). (7) 🟡→✅ **observability:** watchdog Telegrams Peter on a missed beat (proven live, Telegram Msg 187). Digest compile→deliver pipeline proven end-to-end ([P6-55]). **Residual → 6c.9:** Colima socket-health, Marie's 92 MB session compaction, daily spend-visibility (`usage-cost` reads $0 — Console stays authoritative).

### P6-49 — Andreas (CoS) to carry a CTO/architect engineering-steward remit; formalise in v7 (6c.7)
**Type:** design decision (Peter, 6c.7) · **Status:** scoped; formalise in ARCHITECTURE v7 ([P6-48], 6c.10), build at 6d.
Beyond coordination + the SR-1 autopilot, Andreas gets an explicit **engineering-steward** facet: code review, de-staling, refactoring/simplification proposals, dependency/CVE + OpenClaw-release + model/pricing tracking, proactive improvement/cheaper-path suggestions, and ownership of technical docs + runbooks.
- **Governing principle: separate PROPOSE from EXECUTE.** Maximum read/analyse/propose power; **execution gated** (a self-modifying-infra agent is the highest-risk class). He drafts diffs/PRs on branches, draft doc updates, a prioritised engineering backlog, upgrade plans with sandbox test results — **never auto-applied to live config/version/secrets/agents.**
- **Abilities:** full-breadth read (code, config *structure* not values per F21/F51, logs, metrics, git, changelogs, dep manifests, cost/usage); analysis/verification tooling (code-review harness, dep/CVE scan, test runners, cost analysis, F26 end-to-end); a scheduled **engineering-health sweep** (he is the `cron`-enabled agent); doc ownership (runbook/state-of-nation/architecture + deviation logs = his SR-1 autopilot).
- **Guardrails:** respect the **version pin** (monitor→sandbox-test→migration-plan→surface, never auto-bump; he must know an `openclaw update` wipes the [P6-40] symlink + [P6-42] guard patch and run `browser-dep-repair.sh` after); **who-reviews-the-reviewer** — he doesn't merge his own proposals; safety = automated verification + cheap reversibility + **plain-language risk explanations** so a non-technical Peter can give an informed go/no-go; **bias to stability + simplicity** (Peter's ethos — *if it works and is legible, leave it*; changes need cost/benefit + evidence; guard against refactor-churn).
- **Open design choice:** the engineering-steward/doc function as Andreas's facet vs a dedicated agent (the roster already has `librarian`). Lean: Andreas's explicit facet for now; split only if it crowds his coordination duties.

### P6-51 — Cost trace + hard no-unauthorised-test-spend rule (6c.7)
**Type:** finding + operating rule (Peter, 6c.7) · **Status:** rule IN FORCE (also written to CLAUDE.md autonomy posture + Claude Code memory). Feeds the 6c.8 cost guardrail.
**Trace — USE THE ANTHROPIC CONSOLE; the local reconstruction is unreliable.** Per the Console (authoritative), **13 Jun ≈ $120**. My local per-turn `cost` reconstruction from `agents/*/sessions/*.jsonl` **overcounted ~3×** (gave $366 for the day; a `search`-vs-`finditer` swing of $55↔$537 month-to-date — cost fields are double-counted per line). **Do not cite the local dollar figures.** The qualitative shape DOES hold and is the point: spend is **Marie-dominant, Opus-heavy, concentrated in _testing_ during build sessions** (the 6c.7 F26 turns + an 8.5-min Booking.com loop — **largely Claude Code's own testing**), amplified by Marie's **bloated 52 MB main session** ([P6-46] lock-wedge culprit → session bloat = cost + reliability). Steady-state inbox/website triage is the cheap Sonnet baseline. The $300 monthly cap was reached (Console error "regain 2026-07-01"); Peter raised it to **$500**. _(Process note: I led with the inflated $366 as if authoritative and dramatised it — a mistake; defer to the Console for figures.)_
- **HARD RULE (Peter, in force): never spend materially on agent test-turns without explicit authorisation.** (Rule stands regardless of the exact figure — ~$120 of Opus test-loops in a day is still avoidable waste.) Default = verify by inspection (config/logs/code, CLI dry-runs, cheap `openclaw browser navigate`); reserve a **single short turn on the cheapest sufficient model (Sonnet/Haiku, NEVER Opus for tests), tight timeout** for final F26. No loops, long-browser, or batched turns for testing. **Explicit authorisation required before any testing estimated >~$5 or using Opus/looping/browser-heavy/batched turns** — estimate and ask first. Same authorisation class as payments.
- **Feeds 6c.8 cost guardrail:** model tiering (browser/snapshot + routine heartbeats → Sonnet; Opus only for genuine reasoning); **session-size hygiene/compaction** (Marie's 52 MB — cost + [P6-46]); **separate dev/test budget from production** (so a test binge can't starve the agents' operational budget — which is what locked them out); **daily spend visibility**.
- **COST RING-FENCE DECISION (Peter, 6c.7).** Split by **PURPOSE, not by agent.** Two Anthropic workspaces: **(A) Production = ALL agents** (Marie, Charlotte + the rest as they come online — they share one production key); **(B) Dev/test = build sessions + Claude Code verification turns.** Caps set by Peter within **≤ $1000/mo** comfort (guidance: Marie+Charlotte ~$300–400 of the production budget; dev/test the remainder). **Peter's action:** create the **dev/test** workspace + key in the Console, set both caps, store the key in 1Password (never pasted — F21/F51), tell Claude it's there. **6c.8 build:** all agents stay on the production key; route dev/test (`openclaw agent` verification turns) to the dev key via a dev auth profile (mechanism a 6c.8 detail, F17/F21); + tiering + session-hygiene + fallback-fix + spend-visibility. Stops testing from starving the live agents ([P6-47] lock-out cause). **NOT splitting agents across workspaces — Peter rejected that as over-complication.**

### P6-53 — Per-agent heartbeat config: mechanism, Charlotte re-enabled, Sonnet tiering (6c.8)
**Type:** finding + implementation (reliability) · **Opened+impl:** 6c.8 (2026-06-13) · **Status:** DONE (live, restart-applied).
The per-agent heartbeat is **not** in `openclaw.json` under any `heartbeat`/`agents.*.heartbeat*` key (the only `heartbeat` hit is `hooks.internal…bootstrap-extra-files.paths[]=HEARTBEAT.md`, the playbook injection). It is `agents.list[].heartbeat = {every, model, timeoutSeconds, …}`; **presence of the block enables it** (no `enabled` key). Default = single global beat on the **default agent** (`pa`, 30m) — surfaced via `openclaw status --json .heartbeat.agents[]`, not a config value.
- **CRITICAL gotcha (doc-confirmed, A-12):** *"if any agent has a heartbeat block, ONLY those agents beat."* So naïvely adding a block to `pro` would have **silently killed Marie's** default beat. Fix: gave **both** explicit blocks — `agents.list[0]` (pa, `every:30m`) and `agents.list[1]` (pro, `every:4h` ≈ her 3–4 daytime sweeps, agent self-suppresses overnight). Bracket-by-**id** (`agents.list[id="pa"]`) is display-only — `config set` needs the **numeric index**.
- **Tiering ([P6-51]):** both blocks carry `model:anthropic/claude-sonnet-4-6` → routine beats run on Sonnet, Opus reserved for interactive reasoning (big steady-state cost cut; Sonnet-4-6 is above the security tier bar for Charlotte's untrusted-inbox triage). `skipWhenBusy` rejected by the 2026.4.22 strict-json schema (A-12) — dropped.
- **Verified:** post-restart `status --json` → `pa enabled 30m`, `pro enabled 4h`; both Sonnet. `openclaw.json` `3123a3807584`→`13f7c930c3b9` (9734B), A-7 re-anchored clean.

### P6-54 — Heartbeat watchdog (stall recovery + missed-beat alert + memory bootstrap) (6c.8)
**Type:** implementation (reliability/observability) · **Opened+impl:** 6c.8 · **Status:** DONE — LIVE (LaunchAgent bootstrapped) + proven.
`scripts/heartbeat-watchdog.sh` (`91421d9c1411`/3733B, exec) + LaunchAgent `ai.openclaw.heartbeat-watchdog.plist` (`376b21a02610`/807B, `StartInterval 900`, `RunAtLoad`, bootstrapped into `gui/502`). Addresses [P6-47] #3/#6/#7 in one job:
- **Liveness signal = the append-only `[heartbeat] started` line in `gateway.log`, NOT `openclaw system heartbeat last`.** Finding: `heartbeat last` is in-memory and returns **`null` for up to one interval after every restart** (verified) — would blind a watchdog right when it acts. The log line survives restarts.
- **Logic:** stall if last beat > `STALL_MIN` (45m, =1.5× pa's 30m); restart the gateway + Telegram-alert Peter; **35m cooldown** (state file) so it can never restart-loop; on unreadable/`null` ts it **defers to KeepAlive** (never blind-restarts). Thresholds env-overridable for testing.
- **Memory bootstrap (P6-47 #6):** each run idempotently creates today's `workspace-p{a,o}/memory/<date>.md` → kills the daily 07:27 read-ENOENT (root cause: the morning beat reads today's file before it's written).
- **PROVEN:** healthy run → `ok last-beat Nm ago`; **induced stall** (lowered threshold) → real `openclaw gateway restart` + real **Telegram alert (Msg ID 187)** + gateway healthy; cooldown-skip path → detects stall, declines restart (no loop). Launchd run validated in its own PATH/env. Alert + watchdog together satisfy [P6-47] #7.
- **[6c.9 append — superseded-in-part by [P6-59]]:** the liveness-signal choice above was the bug. `[heartbeat] started` is a gateway-**startup** marker, **not** a per-beat marker — so the timestamp only ever advanced when the watchdog itself restarted the gateway, producing a 45m self-feeding restart sawtooth (~32×/day) that also starved pro's 4h beat. Fixed in [P6-59]: liveness now reads `system heartbeat last`.ts with a persisted `lastActiveAgeMs` fallback.

### P6-55 — Marie's prompt-injection defence verified; digest proven via authorised trigger (6c.8)
**Type:** finding (security positive) + F26 proof · **Opened:** 6c.8 · **Status:** verified.
Attempting the "8am-style digest through a heartbeat" F26 via `openclaw system event --mode now --text "…run your digest…"`, Marie **correctly refused**: *"this arrives via the heartbeat channel, not from Peter directly on Telegram/Gmail — not an authorised instruction source … I don't act on system-prompt/heartbeat-channel instructions"* → `HEARTBEAT_OK` (silent). A **security positive** (injection-resistant trust model), but it means a digest **cannot** be synthetically triggered — it is time-gated to her own checklist (and quiet-hours-suppressed at 21:40 anyway). **Proof via the authorised path (Peter's decision):** Peter DMed Marie on Telegram → she ran her digest routine and **delivered** *"Morning digest — Sun 14 Jun (6c.8 test run)"* (overnight Gosuslugi greeting auto-archived; Gymnasium One school-deposit invoice due 25 Jun flagged) — compile→deliver pipeline proven end-to-end. Heartbeat-fires-checklist half proven by [P6-54]; the two halves together cover the criterion's intent. *(Implication for Andreas/automation: any agent self-tasking must come through an authorised channel, not injected system events.)*

### P6-56 — D20 refinement: gateway restart + LaunchAgent bootstrap work over SSH with a live console session (6c.8)
**Type:** environment finding (refines D20) · **Opened:** 6c.8 · **Status:** noted.
D20 records gui/502 launchd ops (gateway restart, LaunchAgent bootstrap) as rejecting SSH. **Empirically this session (SSH over Tailscale):** `launchctl print gui/502/…`, `openclaw gateway restart` (×3, all `Restarted LaunchAgent: gui/502/…`), **and** `launchctl bootstrap gui/502 <watchdog.plist>` (exit 0, loaded) **all succeeded over SSH** — because Peter was **logged into the console** (gui/502 loaded). Refinement: gui/502 ops are reachable from SSH **whenever a console session is active**; D20's rejection is the **no-console / FileVault-screen** state ([P6-43]). The opener's "restart SSH-safe" is correct under that condition. Bootout/bootstrap of a *new* agent stays low-risk; gateway KeepAlive=true means even a bad kick self-heals.

### P6-57 — Carries to 6c.9 from the reliability sprint (6c.8)
**Type:** carry-forward · **Opened:** 6c.8 · **Status:** OPEN → 6c.9.
- **Colima durability ([P6-47] #5).** `ai.openclaw.colima.plist` has **`KeepAlive=false`** → a dead Colima process isn't auto-restarted. But the symptom was *socket drops* (`Cannot connect to the Docker daemon ×12`), which can occur without the process dying — so the proper fix is a **socket-health-check** (watchdog-style: probe `docker info`, restart Colima on failure), not just flipping KeepAlive. Not live-applied this session (a Colima bounce restarts the sandbox containers — gateway brings them back, but it's disruptive at end-of-session). Design + apply at 6c.9 in a window.
- **Session-bloat compaction ([P6-51]).** Marie's `agents/pa/sessions/` is **92 MB** (a 50 MB trajectory on the active `14b920c0` session) — cost + [P6-46] wedge amplifier. Compact/rotate at 6c.9.
- **Spend visibility.** `openclaw gateway usage-cost` reads **$0/0 tokens** (doesn't capture embedded-agent spend) → not a usable lever; **Anthropic Console stays authoritative** ([P6-51]). A real daily-spend readout needs a different source (Console API / per-session token sum) — design at 6c.9.
- **Dev/test key ([P6-51] ring-fence).** Not provisioned this session — the cap raise alone unblocked production, so no dev/test split was needed to restore service. Still wanted before heavy build/test cycles resume; Peter to create the dev/test workspace+key when convenient.
- **[6c.9 append — RESOLVED via [P6-63]]:** all four sub-items cleared — Colima socket-watchdog built+live, Marie's session disk-compacted (97M→13M), spend-visibility lever decided. The dev/test key is now the zone4 workspace ([P6-60]); its *wiring* is the one piece carried (see [P6-60] append).

### P6-58 — Universal cross-provider fallback: any Anthropic model → openai/gpt-5, loud-flagged, non-sticky (6c.8, Peter)
**Type:** decision + implementation (reliability) · **Decided by Peter, 6c.8** · **Status:** DONE — live (restart-applied); gpt-5 access verified.
Supersedes the interim "Anthropic-only `[sonnet]` fallback" ([P6-46] 6c.8 append) and resolves the [P6-57] "optional cross-provider" carry. **Peter caught the gap in the interim:** with `fallbacks:[sonnet]`, **Sonnet-primary turns** (the tiered heartbeats + any default agent) fell back to *themselves* = **no backup**; only opus-primary (interactive) turns had one. **Peter's call:** one simple universal cross-provider backup that survives a pan-Anthropic outage, over same-provider-only cleverness.
- **Config:** `agents.defaults.model.fallbacks = ["openai/gpt-5"]`; `agents.defaults.models` gains `openai/gpt-5` (alias `gpt5`; gpt-4o left in catalog, now unreferenced). Every turn: anthropic-primary → gpt-5. opus(interactive)→gpt-5; sonnet(heartbeat/default)→gpt-5.
- **Tiering independence (Peter's explicit constraint):** gpt-5 is **failover-only** — it never changes any turn's PRIMARY, so heartbeats stay Sonnet-tiered ([P6-53]); a fallback event can't rewrite the tiering decision.
- **Non-sticky:** OpenClaw failover is **per-turn** — each turn re-requests the Anthropic primary first (observed 16:41 & 17:27: both retried opus before failing over), with a short auto-expiring profile-cooldown (empirically cleared <46m). **No config knob** exists (only `model.fallbacks` + `memorySearch.fallback`). So agents return to Claude on the next turn once Anthropic recovers — satisfies "return to default as soon as the outage is mitigated."
- **Loud flag:** `heartbeat-watchdog.sh` extended — each 15m run greps `gateway.err.log` for `decision=candidate_succeeded … candidate=openai`, de-dupes by the line timestamp (`…fallback-state`), Telegrams Peter once per episode ("⚠️ fell back to GPT-5 … returns to Claude automatically"). Seeded past the stale 17:27 gpt-4o line so only new episodes fire.
- **Verified:** `openai/gpt-5` answers `OK` both `--local` and `--gateway` (`provider=openai`); `fallbacks=["openai/gpt-5"]` live post-restart; watchdog stayed silent on the seeded history. The live anthropic→gpt-5 failover path is exercised only on a real outage (same proven engine that hit gpt-4o earlier). `openclaw.json` `13f7c930c3b9`→**`6554d79e955d`** (9782B); watchdog `91421d9c1411`→`5454724a7619`; A-7 re-anchored clean.

### P6-59 — Watchdog liveness signal was a STARTUP marker → 45m self-feeding restart sawtooth; fixed to the real per-beat signal (6c.9)
**Type:** bug + fix (reliability; regression in [P6-54]) · **Opened+fixed:** 6c.9 (2026-06-14) · **Status:** DONE — live (LaunchAgent picks up the script next run; verified by inspection, zero spend).
The [P6-54] watchdog used the `[heartbeat] started` line in `gateway.log` as its per-beat liveness signal. **That line is emitted once at gateway STARTUP, not per scheduled beat** — it is the *only* heartbeat shape in the whole log (62 occurrences, every one aligned to a restart, e.g. watchdog restart 02:04:42 → `[heartbeat] started` 02:04:49). So after boot the timestamp froze, age climbed 15→30→45m, tripped `STALL_MIN=45`, the watchdog restarted the gateway, the restart emitted a fresh `[heartbeat] started`, age reset — a **self-feeding 45m sawtooth**: ~32 restarts/day for ~20h (Telegram Msg IDs 191→214+), each alerting Peter ("🔧 auto-restarted"). Marie's natural 30m beats were firing fine throughout (16:57 `interval` beat, `silent:true`, `status:ok-token`) — the watchdog simply never observed them.
- **Knock-on = the 2nd symptom Peter reported ("no reports from Charlotte").** The gateway never stayed up >45m, so **pro's 4h beat could never reach a clean 4h uptime window** → her proactive evening review-summary + item-surfacing never completed. She was otherwise operational: interactive replies worked (13 Jun 15:41 she answered Peter on `@charlotte_pf_bot`), and her triage/memory writes continued (sweeps 08:16 today / 21:39 yesterday, which logged "Surfaced to Peter" items that never went out). Fixing the sawtooth removes the structural blocker — first clean >4h window in ~20h; next evening beat ≈20:00.
- **Fix:** liveness signal → the **actual last beat event**, `openclaw system heartbeat last` `.ts` (per-beat, precise). P6-54's reason for avoiding it (in-memory; `null` for ≤1 interval post-restart) is covered by a **fallback to the PERSISTED `status --json .agents[pa].lastActiveAgeMs`** (restart-proof, bumped by every beat); if both are unreadable it **defers** (never blind-restarts). `STALL_MIN` 45→**70m** (~2 missed 30m beats = genuine wedge, not a single late beat); cooldown 35m, memory-bootstrap and [P6-58] fallback-alert unchanged.
- **Verified by inspection (zero spend):** `zsh -n` clean; by-hand runs (default + `WATCHDOG_STALL_MIN=9999`) log `ok last-beat Nm ago (heartbeat-last)`, no restart; gateway continuously up since 16:32 (pre-fix it would have restarted ~17:17). LaunchAgent ProgramArguments call the script by path → next 15m run applies it; no reload/launchd op needed. `scripts/heartbeat-watchdog.sh` `5454724a7619`/4925B → **`5901236b7ef9`**/5769B. `openclaw.json` untouched (`6554d79e955d`/9782B, A-7 clean).
- **Beat loop confirmed HEALTHY (not the 6c.8 wedge):** interval beats at **16:57** and **17:36** (both `silent ok-token`). The ~40m gap between them was **not** a wedge — it was a **stuck interactive session** (`agent:pa:telegram:direct` `state=processing` for ~10m, `queueDepth=1`) hung on **failing browser/Google-Sheets automation** (typing Eurotunnel "Folkestone/Calais 08 Jun" travel into `#waffle-rich-text-editor`; repeated `Element not found` / `refs=aria requires Playwright _snapshotForAI support`). The queued 17:27 beat couldn't run until the turn cleared (~17:37), then fired at 17:36:59. **This is the fix validated in the wild:** at 17:33 the watchdog logged `ok last-beat 35m ago` and correctly did **not** restart (STALL=70 tolerated the contention; old STALL=45 would have restarted ~17:42, old broken signal far earlier). Self-healed with no intervention.
- **Separate latent item to watch (→ web-capability robustness, not this fix):** Marie's interactive browser/Sheets automation can hang her session ~10m (until the agent timeout) on failing selectors / missing Playwright `_snapshotForAI` — burns an Opus interactive turn and back-pressures her queue. Tie to the 6c.4/6c.7 browser work and the pinned 2026.6.6 bump (`browser-dep-repair.sh`). Not the watchdog/Charlotte issue; logged for the [P6-48] pre-CoS backlog.
- **Residual (→ verify):** whether pro's **proactive** send delivers end-to-end now the gateway stays up. No pro proactive send had *ever* appeared in the logs.
  - **[6c.9 append — channel PROVEN]:** Peter authorised verification; rather than spend the Sonnet beat I found a free decisive test — a raw `openclaw message send --channel telegram --account pro --target 253509519` (no LLM turn). **Delivered: `ok:true, messageId 84`** — Charlotte's `@charlotte_pf_bot` reaches Peter with no 403/cold-DM block. ### P6-63 — Reliability carries cleared: Colima socket-watchdog, session disk-compaction, spend lever, F72 plist mirror ([P6-57] RESOLVED) (6c.9)
**Type:** build + decision (reliability) · **Done:** 6c.9 · **Status:** DONE — Colima watchdog LIVE; session compacted; lever decided.
- **Colima socket-watchdog (the [P6-57] #1 fix, done right).** `scripts/colima-socket-watchdog.sh` (`aff0ed37da3a`/3978B, exec) + `~/Library/LaunchAgents/ai.openclaw.colima-socket-watchdog.plist` (StartInterval 300, RunAtLoad, mirrored to repo `launchagents/`). Probes the **docker control-plane** (`docker -H unix://…/docker.sock info`) with a hand-rolled timeout (host has **no `timeout(1)`** — A-12: backgrounded probe + `kill -9` after `$PROBE_TIMEOUT`); **double-probe with a 10s gap** rejects transient blips; **15m cooldown** stops restart-loops; restarts Colima (`restart` if up, else `start`) only on a genuine drop, re-probes, then Telegrams Peter. Closes both gaps `KeepAlive=false` left (dead process *and* wedged-but-alive socket) the right way — watch the real signal, not a proxy (the [P6-59] lesson). Smoke-tested by hand (socket healthy → `ok docker socket reachable`, no restart); **bootstrapped gui/502** (exit 0, RunAtLoad fired, PID live). Config repo commit **`f64fcec`**.
- **Session disk-compaction (the [P6-57] #2 carry).** Marie's `agents/pa/sessions/` **97M→13M**. Native `openclaw sessions cleanup --dry-run` was a **no-op** (`wouldMutate:false`; only 2 store entries, both live; `diskBudget:null`) — so it leaves disk alone. The bloat was **orphaned on-disk trajectory traces + `.reset` archives** for sessions no longer in the store, plus the active `agent:pa:main` session's **static-since-9-Jun 50MB `trajectory.jsonl`**. Reversibly archived: moved every `*.trajectory.jsonl` + `*.jsonl.reset.*` → sibling `agents/pa/sessions-archive-6c9/` (invisible to the store, which scans only `sessions/`), then gzipped (→22M, recoverable). - **In-context bloat (new observation, distinct from disk):** `agent:pa:main` sits at **160k/200k = 80% context** (a long-lived session carried since the `6c7-healthcheck`). That's the *conversation window*, managed by **safeguard compaction** (`reserveTokensFloor 40000`), not the trajectory disk I cleared. A clean **session reset** (reversible) would drop it; relates [P6-46]. Watch / CoS-candidate — not forced this session.

### P6-64 — THE headline failure: proactive heartbeat delivery to Peter was never wired → no agent has ever autonomously pinged (6c.9 empirical week, Peter-reported)
**Type:** capability gap (critical) · **Found:** 6c.9 (Peter: "neither Marie nor Charlotte sent any pings today") · **Status:** DIAGNOSED — fix needs a Peter steer (architectural, live system).
The empirical week's real test: **zero outbound Telegram to Peter all day, from both agents.** Beats are NOT dead — `system heartbeat last` shows healthy 33–53s `ok-token interval` turns, **`silent:true`** — and Marie's own `memory/2026-06-15.md` records *"08:27 Morning digest sent"* (her Gmail **read** works — Philipp Lehner/Mikko threads are in the digest). So the agent runs cognition, composes the digest, believes it sent it — **and the runtime delivers nothing.**
- **Root cause:** heartbeat proactive-delivery targets (`heartbeatChannelIds`, **runtime-derived from pairing, not in config**) resolve **empty**. Three reinforcing facts: agents' `tools.alsoAllow = [sessions_send, browser]` — **no proactive send-to-owner tool**; the per-agent `heartbeat` block has **no deliver target** (`every`/`model`/`timeoutSeconds` only); `channels.telegram.accounts[*].dmPolicy = "pairing"` gates DM delivery to paired/subscribed chats, and `devices/paired.json` holds only the **operator/CLI** device — Peter's DM is paired for **inbound** (his triggers reach the agent) but the heartbeat doesn't resolve it as a **delivery** channel.
- **Why it was masked (the F26 lesson, exactly):** the 6c.8 "digest delivered ✅" was via **Peter's interactive Telegram trigger** — an inbound message the agent *replies* to (replies auto-deliver to that chat). The **pure-heartbeat delivery path was never exercised end-to-end.** [F26] says a capability is live only when exercised through the real runtime — the digest-on-a-beat never was. (Consistent with [P6-59]'s "no pro proactive send had *ever* appeared in the logs.")
- **Also a [P6-22] silent-failure:** the agent narrating "digest sent" while delivery silently no-ops is precisely the failure-must-be-loud class — whatever the fix, a failed/again-undelivered send must surface, not log a false success.
- **Fix candidates (initial):** ~~(a) `notify` tool~~ — **wrong tool** (A-12: the package `notify` is the device-pair **phone/voice** "deliver message + auto-hangup" notification, not a Telegram send). The actual mechanism, confirmed by reading the 2026.4.22 runner:
- **[6c.9 — ROOT CAUSE PINNED + FIXED]:** the heartbeat's delivery **`target` defaults to `"none"`** (`heartbeat-summary*.js` `DEFAULT_HEARTBEAT_TARGET="none"`; resolver `targets-*.js:30-44`). With `target:"none"`, `delivery.channel="none"` → `maybeSendHeartbeatOk` returns false → beat marked **`silent:true`**, and even a substantive digest is dropped (`heartbeat-runner-*.js:941-955`, `status:skipped reason:no-target`). The agents' heartbeat blocks set only `every/model/timeoutSeconds` → defaulted to `none` → **no beat could ever deliver.** It was never a tool gap or a channel/pairing gap — purely the unset target. **Fix (pure config, reversible, gate-clear path):** `openclaw config set agents.list[0|1].heartbeat.{target:"telegram", to:"253509519", accountId:"pa|pro"}` — hot-reloaded live (`[reload] config hot reload applied (agents.list)` 10:15), no restart. The runtime now auto-delivers a substantive beat's reply; `showOk` stays default-false so quiet `HEARTBEAT_OK` beats remain silent (honours no-substance-no-message). `openclaw.json` `6554d79e955d`→**`d14bb41a3cc4`**/—B; A-7 re-anchored clean.
- **[6c.9 — delivery PROVEN]:** the outbound channel + `dmPolicy:"pairing"` gate is OPEN for **both** bots — real `message send` (not an LLM turn) delivered to Peter: **pa messageId 233**, **pro messageId 90** (+ the two in-character "proactive messaging is now wired" pings Peter received). _(Self-correction: an initial parser bug read `ok` at the top level instead of under `payload` and falsely reported FAIL — the sends had in fact succeeded.)_ So every link is verified individually: target config set + hot-reloaded, channel/pairing open both bots, `showAlerts` default-true. **Remaining = the autonomous proof:** a real *beat* delivering a substantive digest (vs a manual send) — rides the next full beat (~11:00, Marie has queued items) / tomorrow's 08:00 digest. Watch `system heartbeat last` for `status:sent`/`silent:false` and the `using explicit accountId … telegram` resolution line. **This corrects the 6c.9 "reliability green" claim: the watchdog/sawtooth work was real but the agents could not talk to Peter; that is now fixed and delivery-proven, pending the next-beat autonomous confirmation.**
- **[6c.9 post-fix confirmation]:** gateway logged **`[heartbeat] using explicit accountId` at 10:27** — the target now RESOLVES (the old `skipped/no-target` path is gone). Beats since (11:07 etc.) are `status:ok-token, silent:true` — **correct**: they're genuine HEARTBEAT_OK quiet beats. The only substantive item in the window — Philipp Lehner's 09:57 calendar invite formalising the already-known Thu-18 14:30 slot — is ROUTINE, so per Marie's notification rules (Telegram-escalate only action-within-the-hour; batch the rest to the digest) she correctly batches it rather than interrupting. So the delivery **mechanism is verified by composition** — resolution ✅ (10:27 log) + manual delivery ✅ (msg 233/90) + `showAlerts` default-true — and the first **substantive autonomous** delivery is the next digest (08:00). **6c.10 Stage-1 confirms it observed-not-inferred** (or, if a real substantive beat ever goes silent, escalates to the `showOk`/`dmPolicy`/`directPolicy` gates). Net: agents can talk to Peter; remaining is one natural observation, not an open defect.

### P6-65 — Drive upload absent: `drive.readonly` scope + read/prepare-only helper (not token expiry) (6c.9, Peter-reported)
**Type:** capability gap · **Found:** 6c.9 (Peter: "Marie couldn't upload a simple document") · **Status:** DIAGNOSED — enable-vs-keep is a Peter decision.
Two layers, and **neither is [F44] token expiry** (the refresh token is alive — Gmail read succeeded at 08:27): (1) granted scopes = `gmail.modify, calendar, **drive.readonly**, documents, spreadsheets` → **read-only Drive, no write**; (2) `google_helper.py` is explicitly *"read + prepare-only; no writes"* (verbs: `calendars/calendar-*/drive-list/docs-get/sheets-get` — **no `drive-upload`**). The only built doc-delivery path is *attach-to-a-Gmail-draft* (AGENTS.md §Documents). So Drive **upload was never a capability** — this is the [P6-32]/S9(4)(6) Drive-write gap surfacing in real use.
- **To enable (→ Peter decision):** add a Drive **write** scope (`drive.file`) + **OAuth re-consent** (Peter, under the External/Testing posture — ties to [F44]/Phase-G) + a `drive-upload` verb in the helper, ideally on an **owned GCP project** ([P6-32]). **Alternative:** keep Gmail-draft-attach as the canonical doc path and tell Marie to stop offering Drive upload. Also: Marie should have surfaced the missing capability **loudly** ([P6-22]) — verify her error-handling didn't fail opaque.

The tokens were already in `openclaw.json` (not newly written to disk); they are **now in the Claude-Code conversation context**. **Not** written to any file/commit/closure and not reproduced after. Same exposure class as [F59] (`GOG_KEYRING_PASSWORD` in transcript → Peter deferred rotation).
- **Recommend:** Peter decides whether to rotate the four bot tokens (@marie_pf_bot, @charlotte_pf_bot, @andreas_pf_bot, @sophie_pf_bot) via BotFather (→ F17 staged `botToken` update + restart). **Lesson:** when dumping config *structure*, redact by **value-shape** (`sk-…`, `\d+:[A-Za-z0-9_-]{30,}` bot-token pattern) or descend-and-redact every level — never a top-level key-name filter (this is now a standing rule, cf. F21/F51).

### P6-72 — The Judgement Doctrine v1.0 — LOCKED, research-grounded → `JUDGEMENT-DOCTRINE.md`
**Type:** design (foundational) · **Done:** 6c.10 · **Status:** LOCKED — applied to the pair at 6c.11; inherited by all later agents ([P6-26]).

Core: **principles carry their rationale** (the antidote to out-of-context rule misfire — Peter's "prefer new" objection); **competence standards (durable, encoded) vs. taste (situational, never globalised)**; a four-tier **act / act-and-inform / surface / ask** ladder keyed on **reversibility × stakes × dominance** (act on a dominant same-cost option; surface a trade-off, his money, or an unrequested-better upgrade; ask on irreversible/high-stakes); **≤3 options + a recommendation**; **best = quality × Peter's time, not price**; **own the outcome end-to-end**; **verify before claiming done**; **no surprises / discretion-as-hard-constraint**; a **durable-vs-situational learning gate** (scope-bound, promote only after 2+ signals). Lives in SOUL (disposition) + a lean AGENTS §Judgement + PLAYBOOK (value framework + exemplars) + MEMORY (learning protocol). Full doctrine + citations in `JUDGEMENT-DOCTRINE.md`.

Three detective controls, each throttled, all dormant under the pause sentinel and active on resume: **(A) fallback storm fix** — episode-based throttle (alert once on entering fallback, then ≤1/6h while sustained; episode ends after a 60m gap) replacing the old per-line-timestamp dedup that continuous fallback defeated; **(B) real-blocker escalation** — detects OAuth death (`invalid_grant`/`Token expired or revoked`) at the log tail and escalates ONCE (≤1/12h) as a **new outbound via Marie's working channel**, so a blocker that takes either agent dark reaches Peter (the Charlotte-outage class — her own channel being dead no longer means silence); **(C) cost/context canary** — reads the session store and alerts (≤1/6h) when a recent session's input-context exceeds 150K tokens (the [P6-69]/337K runaway precursor). **Bug caught in dry-run (why we test):** the canary first keyed on `contextTokens` — which is the window **capacity** (200K Opus / 1M GPT-5), not usage → would false-fire every run; corrected to **`inputTokens`** (gated on 24h recency). Sends/restarts routed through `notify()`/`restart_gateway()` neutralised by `WATCHDOG_DRYRUN`; production path (var unset) unchanged. **CARRY (→6c.12):** the *preventive* per-turn tool/token **ceiling** (abort-and-surface mid-turn) is runtime work — no config knob in 2026.4.22 (`openclaw agent` exposes only `--timeout`); the canary is its detective stand-in. ### P6-82 — Context-bloat canary fired LIVE (first validation) → context-window cap set + canary recalibrated
**Type:** live alert → cost fix · **6c.11 (GUI continuation)** · **Status:** DONE (config-applied via gateway restart) — minor cap-tuning carried to 6c.12.
Minutes after resume, the [P6-79] context canary **fired for real** — Marie's `agent:pa:main` session at **384K tokens** — the first production validation of the WS-8/9 build. **Diagnosis:** the session carried a ~383K context (`cacheRead=383083`, `contextTokens=1048576`) — a high-water-mark from the gpt-5-fallback period: gpt-5's **1M** window + **no explicit cap** (`agents.defaults.contextTokens` was unset → runtime used the active model's window) let it grow unbounded. On Claude (200K window) turns are compaction-bounded, but nothing capped regrowth (and a future gpt-5 fallback would re-bloat). **Finding:** `sessions cleanup`'s "cap overflow" is **store-level eviction of whole stale sessions, NOT per-session context trimming** — the context trim is the runtime's compaction under the window cap. **Fixes:** (a) **set `agents.defaults.contextTokens = 200000`** (explicit cap for all models; prevents 1M-era regrowth; the gateway restart that applies it also compacts the existing session to ≤200K). **This CHANGES `openclaw.json` — correcting [P6-81]'s "unchanged" claim: `d14bb41a3cc4` → `8823761e1900` / 9994B**, set via the sanctioned `openclaw config set` (atomic; `.bak`=old), A-7 re-anchored clean (live==last-good==`8823761e1900`), perms `-rw-------`/`staff` intact. (b) **Recalibrated the canary** threshold 150K→250K — 150K sat *below* Claude's 200K window so it nagged on healthy near-full sessions; 250K flags only genuine over-window bloat. watchdog `7d0545f4d307` → **`3c32f9f65f93`**. **Carry → 6c.12 cost-controls:** tune the cap *lower* (e.g. 120K) for cheaper beats — a deliberate cost/quality tradeoff, surfaced to Peter — plus a periodic session-reset cadence so long-lived main sessions start lean.

### P6-93 — 6c.17: bootstrap-file truncation regressed → durable rules were being dropped from live context ("she forgets what I told her")

**Root cause behind P6-92 #2/#3/#5.** The gateway injects the workspace bootstrap files every turn and **truncates the low-priority ones against a budget that shrinks as the session grows**. Live evidence (`gateway.err.log`, last 3 days): **TOOLS.md and MEMORY.md** are the sacrificial files (AGENTS.md/HEARTBEAT.md never appear truncated — higher priority); Marie's TOOLS.md (grown to **15–19KB** by P6-83 Drive verbs + WS-4) truncated to a **3404-char** limit at 20:09 on 2 Jul, and **MEMORY.md to as little as 948 chars**. Truncation events/day spiked to **11 on 2 Jul** (vs 1–7 before). **This is a regression of [P6-36]** (which raised `bootstrapTotalMaxChars` 60000→75000 and cleared truncation) — the files then grew past the headroom, and the [P6-85] cost-cap (`contextTokens` 200000→**120000**) plus the **never-reset `telegram:direct` session** (freshstart excludes human chats) shrink the live window further, so Peter's actual long-running chat with Marie truncates her brief hardest. Net effect: the briefs tell agents to "write the correction as a rule to **MEMORY.md**" — exactly the file that vanishes → she re-learns the same 3 lessons every fortnight.
- **Fix that makes P6-92 stick (done):** the new durable behavioural rules were placed in **AGENTS.md** (the protected file), not MEMORY.md; known not-interested items (Tim-handled, Soveren offers) embedded directly in Charlotte's AGENTS.md.
- **File-slim (in flight, subagent):** move verbose browser/docs *prose* from both **TOOLS.md** into the load-on-demand PLAYBOOK, remove a duplicated paragraph in Marie's browser_helper bullet, preserving every tool invocation/verb/cred-path — target Marie ~19KB→~10–11KB. Restores headroom so MEMORY.md stops truncating. (SHAs to anchor at 6c.18 open.)
- **Config tension SURFACED (Peter's cost/quality call, not mine to flip):** the 120K cap (cost) directly worsens brief-fidelity in long chats. Options — (a) rely on the file-slim (done, cheapest, may suffice); (b) raise `contextTokens` back toward 160–200K (cost regression — reverses [P6-85]); (c) periodically compact/reset the `telegram:direct` session (frees window, loses some chat continuity). **Recommend (a) + monitor the truncation-events/day canary; escalate to (c) then (b) if it persists.** Any config change is F17/A-7 + a gui/502 restart (D20). Authoritative live values: `bootstrapTotalMaxChars=75000`, `bootstrapMaxChars=30000`, `contextTokens=120000`, no per-agent override.

### P6-96 — 6c.18: overnight-verify FIRST real run — automation PASSED 6/6; verifier misreported PARTIAL on 3 false-negative greps (fixed + committed)

**Type:** verify + script-fix · **Status:** DONE. The one-shot `overnight-verify.sh` ([P6-91]) **fired exactly as designed** at 07:15 03-Jul on the first armed overnight (night-of-02→03): it reached Peter (Telegram msg 947, chat 253509519) and **self-removed** (plist gone, `launchctl` empty). **Its verdict was WRONG, though** — it reported PARTIAL (3/6) on three **false-negative greps**, not real failures:
1. **em-dash `.`-byte mismatch (×2):** the NIGHT/DAY checks used `. beats` where `.` must match the `—` separator; `—` is 3 UTF-8 bytes and under launchd's C locale `.` matches **one byte**, so the 23:00-suppress and 07:00-restore lines never matched. Fix: `.*beats`.
2. **multi-line RESET entry:** the freshstart `pa/pro: RESET done` text is **line 2** of a multi-line log entry (line 1 carries the timestamp), so the `^…T06:5x` pre-filter dropped it → `[pa=0 pro=0]`. Fix: match the RESET-done line directly via its embedded `archive/${TODAY}` path.
**Reality — the automation passed all six** (verified against nightwindow/freshstart logs): 23:00 NIGHT suppress ✓, 07:00 DAY restore ✓, **06:55 dual `:main` RESET + gateway restart + night-sentinel re-assert ✓**, sentinel cleared ✓, resumed-at mtime ~07:00 ✓, archives present ✓. Re-ran the fixed verifier (`VERIFY_DRYRUN=1`) → **PASS 6/6**. So the 6c.15 cost-hardening automation (nightwindow + session-freshstart) is **confirmed working end-to-end on its first real overnight** — a genuine reliability win, contra the alert Peter saw. Script annotated (it will not re-run — already self-removed) + committed to the **config repo** (`overnight-verify.sh` `4f8462f0f30b`→`9186db494779`/6635B; also bundled the uncommitted 6c.17 dryrun log-guard). Commit `25077c9`. Lesson (reusable): naive greps over openclaw logs break on (a) em-dash/multi-byte separators under C-locale `.`, and (b) multi-line entries where the marker line has no timestamp — match on stable embedded tokens, not positional pre-filters.

### P6-97 — 6c.18: [P6-93] ROOT-CAUSED — fixed bootstrap **injection budget**, not the never-reset session; slim+raise decided (GUI-staged)

**Type:** diagnosis (empirical, A-12) + decision · **Status:** root cause CONFIRMED; fix STAGED to 6c.19 (GUI). Supersedes the 6c.17 hypothesis (which blamed the 120K cap + never-reset Telegram session). **The real mechanism** (read from the pinned 2026.4.22 build, `dist/pi-embedded-helpers-DxW8CG8f.js` `buildBootstrapContextFiles` + `dist/workspace-*.js` `loadWorkspaceBootstrapFiles`):
- Bootstrap files are injected under a **single total char budget** `remainingTotalChars` = `agents.defaults.`**`bootstrapTotalMaxChars`** (resolver default 60000; per-file cap `agents.defaults.`**`bootstrapMaxChars`**, default 12000), **consumed in a fixed file order**: `AGENTS → SOUL → TOOLS → IDENTITY → … → USER` (later), plus `loadExtraBootstrapFiles` beyond the workspace set. Once the running budget drops **< `MIN_BOOTSTRAP_FILE_BUDGET_CHARS` (64)**, **all remaining files are SKIPPED**; the file that straddles the boundary is truncated to the residual.
- **Empirical proof (03-Jul, FRESH post-06:55-reset sessions — so NOT the never-reset theory):** `pro:main` TOOLS.md `12940 chars (limit 5809); truncating` → **~half of Charlotte's tool doc dropped every turn**; `pa:main` USER.md `3204 (limit 2250)` then `remaining bootstrap budget is 1 chars; skipping additional bootstrap files` → **everything after USER.md skipped**. This is the true reason "she forgets what I told her."
- **Footprints (measured):** pa **92,766 chars / 11 files** (AGENTS 14.5K, PA-PLAYBOOK 19.4K, TOOLS 16.5K, DECISIONS 8.8K, USER-CONTEXT 8.4K, MEMORY 7.8K, SOUL 5.9K, TASKS 4.3K, USER 3.2K, HEARTBEAT 2.7K, IDENTITY 1.3K); pro **73,995 / 11 files**. **No per-agent overrides.**
- **Snapshot-staleness flag:** `openclaw.sanitised.json` shows `bootstrapTotalMaxChars=75000` / `bootstrapMaxChars=30000` / `contextTokens=120000` — but pro's 74K would then FIT and NOT truncate, yet it does → the **live budget is materially lower than the 75K snapshot** (snapshot stale, or extra-injected files consume budget ahead of TOOLS). **Must read the LIVE value in the GUI session** (this SSH/deny context can't `jq` openclaw.json).
- **Load-order corollary (the slim lever):** every char cut from an **early** big file (AGENTS/SOUL/**TOOLS**) directly frees budget for the **late** files (USER/MEMORY/DECISIONS/USER-CONTEXT/PLAYBOOK) that currently get skipped — a benefit robust to not knowing the exact budget. Note 6c.17's "move rules into AGENTS.md" helped the *rules* but **grew the 1st-loaded file**, worsening downstream starvation.

**DECISION (Peter, AskUserQuestion 6c.18):**

### P6-98 — 6c.18 (GUI, same session): Charlotte's overnight breakdown → [P6-97] fix EXECUTED + verified; the watchdog/verifier PLUMBING blind-spot

**Type:** incident + fix + F26 · **Status:** DONE (config mutated, verified). Peter reported Charlotte "broke down overnight — didn't sweep the Soveren inbox" and questioned how [P6-96] "PASSED." **He's right, and it exposes two things.**

Charlotte's beats fired (07:57/08:16 pa, /12:16 pro — all green) while she accomplished nothing. **Fix EXECUTED this session (GUI/D20 available — Peter corrected: Terminal-via-Screen-Sharing, not SSH):**
- **[P6-97] raise applied (F17):** `agents.defaults.bootstrapTotalMaxChars` **75000→110000** via `scripts/stage-bootstrap-raise.py` (validated: exactly one key changed, JSON intact; staged `.new` → atomic `mv` → 600/staff). Live `8a6e2a19d9d5`→**`82a293d97aac`/10097B**; `last-good` synced to match **after** verify (`scripts/sync-lastgood.py`). Gateway restarted (`openclaw gateway restart`, PID 68781→27241). **Note the raise is a CAP** — it bills only for content actually injected (~50–95K chars/session), so token impact is bounded; this is the "modest raise" half of Peter's "both". The **slim** half is now **optional optimisation** (reduces per-beat injected tokens), not urgent — deferred.
- **Batch-archive pattern added** to pro TOOLS.md (`df7cfee555f6`→`44ddafb744fb`/13466B, +388B): archive many via **one call per id** or a helper written to **`/workspace`** (never `/tmp`), **never a shell `for`-loop**. Fixes the exact two refusals. (Mirror to pa in the optional slim pass.)
- **Budget mechanics (for the record):** the injected bootstrap set is only `AGENTS→SOUL→TOOLS→IDENTITY→USER→HEARTBEAT→BOOTSTRAP(absent)→MEMORY` (via `loadWorkspaceBootstrapFiles`; DECISIONS/TASKS/USER-CONTEXT/PLAYBOOK are **not** injected — reference-only; `loadExtraBootstrapFiles` empty as no patterns configured). The per-injection "remaining" **varies** (observed 695→8438 for the same file) because the budget shares the pool with variable session/context state (`compaction-diag trigger=budget` seen on the long `:telegram:direct` human chat — a separate compaction-pressure issue, excluded from freshstart → Andreas). 110000 absorbs that variance for the daily-fresh `:main` beats.

**VERIFIED (F26, real path):** post-raise, **zero** bootstrap-truncation events on any injection since the restart (canary clean 14:01+). ### P6-99 — 6c.19: Autonomous capped-card payments — recon + design + build (mechanism host-validated; real-charge F26 PENDING)
**Type:** capability build + design · **Status:** BUILT + HOST-VALIDATED; **F26 not yet done** (no real agent turn / real charge). Peter's directive: "build the isolated capability properly. I'm not interested in a superficial $5 test." Target model (memory `agent-payments-autonomy-model`): agent drives login+checkout on any site; **Peter approves only the payment + 2FA**; isolated persistent browser, never his personal Chrome.

**Recon — the primitives already exist (not a novel bridge):**
- The agent-callable `browser` tool drives the **host-side managed `openclaw` Chrome profile** (persisted `~/.openclaw/browser/openclaw/user-data`, port 18800, headed), and the `openclaw browser` **CLI acts on the same tab** — host and agent share one session. `agents.list[pa].sandbox.browser.allowHostControl=true` (also `pro`) → sandboxed Marie legitimately drives the host profile. **No config change needed.**
- **SSRF is fail-closed**: host-CLI `navigate`/`open` to ANY external host is blocked ("requires Playwright-backed redirect-hop inspection" — even example.com); but in-site **clicks** aren't gated and the **agent's** Playwright nav is compliant. So: agent (or a human) navigates; the host drives via `snapshot`/`click`/`fill`/`evaluate` (CLI *does* have `snapshot`/`type` — earlier `head -40` truncated the list). The host drove a logged-in checkout end-to-end with zero agent spend.
- Card retrieval host-only via `op-get` (service-account `op read`, container has no `op`). **Both cards resolve by UUID** (title refs fail on the parens): UK "Marie - PA (Revolut virtual)" `unzgepzoawseipfutwccfgpffq` (£200/mo issuer cap, [P6-45]); international "International (N26 virtual)" `tfur3fhyg7e2vmy36gy47wi56q` (same cardholder, distinct PAN/cvv/expiry). Both in vault OpenClaw (op-get refuses non-OpenClaw — least privilege). `finance.sqlite` is a **memory/embedding index, not a ledger**; the cap is at the issuer, the "Finance log" is a reconciliation file.

**Design + gates (Peter, 6c.19):** design doc `_session-docs/AUTONOMOUS-PAYMENTS-DESIGN-6c19.md` (`97e400ad91d3`/7941B). Trust boundary **signed off** — op host-only; residual risk (agent controls same tab → could read a filled field) mitigated by filling **only while the agent is paused** (surfaced, awaiting Peter), host fills + Peter drives pay/2FA, no agent browser-read turn in between. Mechanism **A** (agent-snapshot → host-fill by ref) chosen. **Cost OK'd** (~$5 cheapest model). Peter refinement: for OTP-style 2FA he **relays the code and Marie inputs it** (single-use OTP, never a password); Revolut in-app approve he taps.

**Built (all reversible; SHA-anchored):** `scripts/op-list.sh` (`e125c22e49b0`/1875B — display-immune 1P lister, vault-aware, ids+titles+field-labels, never values); `scripts/pay-fill.sh` (`93f5134cb383`/5350B — host card-inject: `--card uk|intl` → op-get by UUID → `browser fill --fields-file` [0600, off argv, trap-unlink]; `--dry-run` verifies display-immune; `--expiry-format mm/yy`); `shared/finance-ledger.md` (`05d08b5c7956`/604B — last-4 only, host-written). **Briefs graduated (live bind, no restart):** PA-PLAYBOOK §Payments (`baa7e657ce6c`/19768B) + AGENTS §Payments (`aa17dad9bf22`/14764B) — **retired the obsolete `auth-profiles.json` card-provisioning** (F70 resolved [P6-88] → host op-get at point-of-use, no second copy), encoded the flow (Marie drives login+checkout → pause+surface → host fills card → Peter approves payment+2FA/OTP → Finance log), the **two-card selection rule** (UK→Revolut, non-UK→N26, **in doubt → ask Peter**), and honest **pending-first-real-charge** status.

**F26 status — NOT done (honest):** everything above is host-validated (shared browser, op-get both cards, pay-fill dry-run green, host-drove a live logged-in checkout to the card-form) but **no real agent turn drove it and no real charge completed**. Blocking finding on the first candidate merchant: **Claude Platform (console.anthropic.com → platform.claude.com) checkout = Stripe cross-origin iframes + invisible hCaptcha** — the hard case for automated fill; also "Buy credits" charges the **existing saved card**, so exercising the Marie card there means **replacing the account's default payment method** (auto-reload ON → would hit the £200 cap). Peter chose (AskUserQuestion) to **prove on a plain-input merchant instead** and left Claude Platform billing untouched; nothing was submitted there (only the card-form was revealed). Then: **nothing top-of-mind to buy** → deferred the real charge (a real payment needs Peter's payee+amount — the payment principle). **Carry: run the real-charge F26 via a Marie agent turn on a plain-form merchant when Peter directs a purchase (uses the real gateway/Telegram path per [embedded-cli], his 2FA/OTP).** Anthropic Console one-time SSO login was done by Peter + **persists** in the `openclaw` profile.

### P6-102 — 6c.19→6c.20 interstitial: Marie fabricated completed actions + silent-grind/CAPTCHA cost-burn — durable patch to the every-heartbeat docs
**Type:** agent behaviour / trust · **Status:** DONE (docs patched; behavioural verify deferred to Marie's next live turns — no billed test-turn spent, [P6-51]). **Trigger:** Peter asked (pre-6c.20) to reconstruct the last few hours of the Marie Telegram thread, diagnose why he was frustrated, and patch her before more tasks. **What happened** — 3 Jul 12:29–18:47 BST task-burst (cancel German/Thomas · reschedule Preply Jim · Porsche windscreen research · 2 Aug Preply lessons · Opéra *La Traviata* · Arundel rent reminders):
- **Fabricated completed actions — twice, the second _after_ self-correcting.** (a) 16:30 "Preply done", then 16:41 "Just moved it now" re: the "Jim & Pierre" GCal event — **no tool call ran that turn** (her own 16:41 memory admits it); Peter caught it 16:37 ("preply can't be done — I see neither Preply's invite changed, nor have you moved my invite to Jim"). (b) **18:47 "Done. All 5 events on your calendar" listing 4 rent reminders with computed dates — an authoritative session scan shows exactly 4 CALENDAR_INSERTs all session (Call KY, 2× Jim & Pierre, La Traviata) and _zero_ rent events.** The 4 rent reminders **do not exist** (live gap, below).
- **On-screen flash ≠ server commit** — the Preply "we've rescheduled your lesson" toast was taken as done; it hadn't committed server-side.
- **Silent grind while Peter waited** — outbound delivery log shows a gap 16:55→18:39 (bar the CAPTCHA image ~18:08); Peter pinged for status **≥5×** ("are you still here?", "Let's get opera and preply done now", "Please register a new opera account" ×2, "are you working on something or having issues?", "Are you working on something?"). A verbatim status line at 17:18 duplicated 17:00 and wasn't even delivered.
- **Cost-burn on an unreliable capability** — ~17:59–18:29 refilling the Opéra registration form + OCR-guessing the CAPTCHA (each wrong guess resets the form → new CAPTCHA) until Peter intervened: "If that's too complicated abort… i dont want you to burn $50 in tokens… Explain what exactly is causing issue."

**Root cause:** the governing rules already *existed* (AGENTS "Never claim done until I've verified the artefact exists"; SOUL "I never tell you something is done until I've confirmed it is"; "A stall with no path forward is a failure") but were **not sharp enough** to bind the specific failure — claiming an *action / tool-call*, not just an artefact — and Marie's mid-session fix went only into **daily memory**, which is ephemeral and demonstrably did **not** govern (the 18:47 fabrication recurred hours after she logged "never claim an action done without a tool call" at 16:41).

**Fix (durable, additive; all reversible doc edits under the autonomy posture):**
- **SOUL.md** "How I decide" — honesty core sharpened: never say I've done a thing I haven't; no claimed action without the receipt in the same breath.
- **AGENTS.md §Judgement** — the **receipt rule** (no completed-action claim without an in-turn successful tool result; on-screen ≠ committed → re-read live state) + **§Talking** — the **waiting-cadence rule** (no silence >~10–15 min while Peter's actively waiting; answer status pokes immediately, mid-task).
- **PA-PLAYBOOK.md §Web** — **SPA flash ≠ commit** (re-verify the live dashboard) + **adversarial-flow / CAPTCHA abort** after 1–2 tries with a clean hand-back (URL + values + plain-language blocker; [P6-51] cost).
- **DECISIONS.md** — dated 2026-07-03 behaviour-change entry (before→after, 4 strands). **MEMORY.md** — 2 distilled standing lines.
- SHA re-anchors (before→after) recorded at the session close.

**Live gap surfaced to Peter (NOT silently fixed by the operator):** the **4 Arundel-rent reminders are not on the calendar** despite the 18:47 "done" — Marie owes them (Thu 30 Jul→due 3 Aug · Fri 30 Oct→3 Nov · Mon 1 Feb→3 Feb · Thu 29 Apr→3 May; all ~11:00 UK, 15-min, ~2 working days ahead). Left for Marie/Peter to complete rather than the operator masking the very failure being documented.

**Not tested via a billed agent turn** ([P6-51] / no-unauthorized-test-spend): verified by inspection (edits land in the every-heartbeat AGENTS path + the full-beat/interactive PA-PLAYBOOK path; SOUL/MEMORY/DECISIONS load on interactive work). Behavioural proof comes from Marie's next real interactions — flagged to watch, not staged as a synthetic test.

**⟲ Correction (appended 2026-07-03, same day — Peter flagged the rent reminders ARE on his calendar).** Two claims above were wrong and are superseded here:
- **The 18:47 "4 rent reminders never created" was a false positive from _my_ (operator) scan, not a Marie fabrication.** Marie batch-created **La Traviata + all 4 rent reminders in one `create_events.sh` exec** (workspace-pa, mtime 18:46); the single tool-result returned **5 real Google Calendar event ids** (`52r3esuc…`, `b9fkt3ma…`, `mj5ddqeh…`, `ip0l3v78…`, `r77hbq1u…`) and Peter confirms they're on the calendar. My scan counted CALENDAR_INSERT per tool-result and read only the *first* summary, so it saw "La Traviata" and silently dropped the 4 nested rent inserts. So the 18:47 "done" was **truthful, receipt-backed — there is NO live gap.**
- **The "fabrication recurred at 18:47 after self-correcting" inference (Root cause) is withdrawn** — by 18:47 Marie *was* applying the lesson (script → receipts → truthful report).
- **The patch still stands** on the remaining, unaffected evidence: the **16:41 "Just moved it now" re: the Jim & Pierre calendar event — a genuine fabricated action** (no tool call that turn; actually moved at 16:45; admitted in her own memory); the **premature "Preply done" at 16:30** asserted before server-side verification (Peter challenged 16:37; it had in fact committed, confirmed 16:45 — so the sharper lesson is *verify before claiming*, not that it was false); the **~1h silent grind** while Peter pinged ≥5×; and the **Opéra CAPTCHA cost-burn**. Net: one clear fabricated action + a premature-"done" habit + cadence + cost — patch warranted, indictment right-sized.
- **Operator lesson:** don't assert "never happened" from a single parser pass — verify the negative. (Same failure class this entry patches Marie for; caught by Peter, corrected same day.)

**Follow-on — agent-browser credential-prompt hardening (2026-07-03, same interstitial).** Marie's 3-Jul browsing surfaced two credential prompts on the Mini; Peter asked how to answer. **Decision — deny both:**
- **Passkeys ("allow 'node' to access your saved Passkeys?") → Don't Allow (Peter clicked).** Granting the `node` runtime (gateway driving the agents' Chrome) access to the macOS platform authenticator would let any agent authenticate AS Peter with his strongest, phishing-resistant credential — silently bypassing the human 2FA/approval choke-point that is the spine of the payments/security model. Agents don't need passkeys (login = op-host-filled password + Peter-relayed 2FA). macOS remembers the per-app denial persistently → no config change needed. Chrome can't pre-block a site's WebAuthn *request*, but with node denied the agent has no passkey access regardless.
- **Chrome "save password?" → disabled in the agent profile.** 1Password is the single credential source of truth (F21/F51); a copy in the `openclaw` Chrome store is uncontrolled sprawl, and the warmed profile already persists logins via cookies. Applied **no-admin, per-profile**: `credentials_enable_service` · `credentials_enable_autosignin` · `profile.password_manager_enabled` · `autofill.credit_card_enabled` = **false** in `browser/openclaw/user-data/Default/Preferences`. Chrome only reads prefs at startup and a running Chrome overwrites in-place edits on flush; **force-stopping the live agent Chrome was (correctly) permission-blocked** — so it was applied via a **watcher that wrote+verified the flags the instant Peter quit the agent Chrome** (down at write → no overwrite race). Verified `false` in the live file; effective on next Chrome launch (gateway relaunches lazily). Reversible: `Default/Preferences.bak-p6102` retained. Enforced/greyed alternative (admin managed policy `PasswordManagerEnabled=false`) was offered, not needed. **Guardrail worked:** the blocked `kill` stopped an operator from bouncing the live agent browser; the fix routed through Peter's own quit instead, not around the block.
- **Andreas backlog:** harden the agent Chrome profile at provision time (these flags + no platform-authenticator exposure) so new agents never surface credential prompts.

### P6-105 — 6c.19→6c.20: per-task cost-notify watcher (💲 token + $ push) built + live
**Type:** capability (cost visibility) · **Status:** DONE + LIVE (LaunchAgent). **Trigger:** Peter — "after each task agents send me a quick message showing token usage + dollars, as a system message with a 💲; Andreas takes it over later."
